рдИрд│рд┐рд╖реНрд╡’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреГрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдордирд╛ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рдЙрд╖реНрдгрд┐рдХреН рдЫрдиреНрджрдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН-тАЩ рдИрд│рд┐рд╖реНрд╡ рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдордирд╛ рд╡реИрдпрд╢реНрд╡ рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореМрд╖реНрдгрд┐рд╣рдВ рд╣’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХ рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпреЗ рдХреНрд░рддрд╛рд╡реМрд╖реНрдгрд┐рд╣реЗ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗ рдЪреЗрджрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ- рдИрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рд╛ рд╣реАрддреНрдпреМрд╖реНрдгрд┐рд╣рдореН’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рек. резрей) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

+Jamison Brereton

23 (643)
Agni
Vi┼Ыvamanas Vaiya┼Ыva
30 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, arranged in trcas ╠е
The poet begins the hymn by urging himself to perform his sacrificial tasks (vss. 1тАУ2ab), ending this little section with vocatives addressed to himself but seem ingly designed to identify himself with his divine target Agni: тАЬbelonging to all domainsтАЭ is often an epithet of Agni (as well as of Indra) and тАЬhaving all in mindтАЭ (vi┼Ыva╠Бmanas) could be a divine descriptor. However, at least according to the Anukramaс╣З─л, it is the poetтАЩs own name, and he then (vs. 2c) speaks in his own 1st-person voice. This interactive quality is prominent throughout the hymn. The poetтАЩs self-address returns in verse 24, and in between he also addresses in the 2nd person plural the assembled priests and worshipers, on whose behalf he is work ing (vss. 7тАУ9; see esp. 9a, where he calls them тАЬseekers of the truthтАЭ). (On poetic self-address see Jamison 2009a.) AgniтАЩs role in this social context, as clanlord of

clans, is also emphasized (vss. 10, 13тАУ14, 20). Manu, the mythical founder of the larger ─Аrya sacrificial community known as the тАЬdescendants of Manu,тАЭ is also duly remembered (vss. 13, 17, 25тАУ26), as are the mythical seer U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya (vs. 17) and the poetтАЩs immediate ancestor, the seer Vya┼Ыva (vss. 16, 23), whose devo
tion to Agni and lucrative relationship with his patron, Ukс╣гan, merit mention and provide a model for Vaiya┼ЫvaтАЩs own gentle hint to his patron Varo Suс╣г─Бman (vs. 28). Thus the poet situates his praise of the god and his requests to him in a web of social relations and mutual dependency pertaining both in the current time and in the long history of the descendants of Manu.
Both the praise and the requests follow the common tropes of the genre, though often nicely executed. The focus is on Agni as the messenger of the gods and as the carrier of our oblations to them. Some of the tr╠еcas show thematic or syntactic unity (e.g., vss. 13тАУ15 against demons and cheats), but the tr╠еca structure is not prominent, and there are bridges across tr╠еcas (e.g., the messenger theme in vss. 18тАУ19).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAdore him who resists (our foes), worship J─Бtavedas the diffuser of smoke, of unobstructed radiance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who resists: prat─лvyam = ┼Ыatruс╣гu pratigamana ┼Ы─лlam agnim: Agni, who has he property of going againstenemies

+Jamison Brereton

Reverently invoke him to receive (our offerings); sacrifice to J─Бtavedas, possessing curling smoke and flames that cannot be grasped,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn begins with a h├н clause. Flg. JPB, the h├н signals that the action in this clause precedes and forms the basis of the action in b.

On prat─лvy├аm see Scarlatta 500.

+Griffith

WORSHIP thou Jatavedas, pray to him who willingly accepts,
Whose smoke wanders at will, and none may grasp his flame.

+Geldner

So berufe denn den Opferdarbringer, verehre den Jatavedas, des Rauch wallend und des Flamme unfa├Яbar ist,

+Grassmann

Auf, preise ihn, der gern empf├дngt, den Wesenkenner ehre recht, Dess Rauch aufwirbelt, dessen Licht unfassbar ist.

English translation:

тАЬCommend with praise, all-beholding Vi┼Ыvamanas, that Agni, who is the giver of chariots to theunenvious (worshipper).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

To Agni the giver, with your hymn, o you common to all domains, who have all in mind [/Vi┼Ыvamanas (=the poet)].
And I shall praise the competitors [=flames], (drivers) of chariots,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner I take ab as a continuation of vs. 1, with c starting a new clause.

The vocc. in ab are the self-address of the poet, as in VIII.22.1-2. Here the poet first exhorts himself with 2nd ps. imperatives (1ab) and then switches to a pseudo-modal 1st ps. -se in c. The first voc. vi┼Ыvacarс╣гaс╣Зe (2a) is a bit of a red herring, since this stem is otherwise used of gods. But he addresses and thus identifies himself with his speaking name Vi┼Ыvamanas in b, making it clear that he was simply appropriating the divine epithet for himself.

I supply v├бhn─лn to govern r├бth─Бn─Бm in c, on the basis of v├бhniс╕е in 3c and v├бhn─л r├бth─Бn─Бm in VIII.94.1. I surmise that this is also RenouтАЩs thinking behind тАЬ(comme conducteurs) des chars,тАЭ though he makes no comment.

+Griffith

Thou, all men’s friend, Visvamanas, exaltest Agni with thy song,
The Giver, and his flames with which no cars contend.

+Geldner

Den Geber Agni mit Lobrede, du allbekannter Visvamanas, und preise die wetteifernden Rosse der Wagen,

+Grassmann

Den Geber, allbeliebter du, den Agni r├╝hm mit deinem Lied Und die wie Wagen rennenden, Vi├зvamanas!

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe repeller (of foes), the glorified by hyms, arrests the food and drink, and the bearer of oblationstakes away the wealth (of those) of whom he foreknows (the neglect of sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Takes away the wealth:upavid─Б vindate vasu: upavedana = by proximate knowing, i.e. ete hav─лс╣Гс╣гi dev─Бrtham naprayacchant─лtyetaj├▒─Бnena teс╣г─Бm eva dhanam labhate; “these do not give oblations to the gods; by thisknowledge he takes their ealth; those non- sacrificers, whose food and its juices are arrested, their wealth, too,he takes away by his divine knowledge (of their guilt)”

+Jamison Brereton

Whose onward thrust, worthy of verses, (aims) to seize refreshments and nourishments.
By close searching the driver [=Agni] finds the goods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (n. 3c) takes upav├нd─Б тАж vindate as simply equivalent to upavindate, which is esp. puzzling because ├║pa is not otherwise construed with тИЪvid in the RV.

My тАШcloseтАЩ in the tr. тАШclose searchingтАЩ is meant to convey the intimate nuance of this preverb.

Note the v alliteration in c: upav├нd─Б v├бhnir vindate v├бsu.

Through whose discovering power the priest obtaineth wealth.

Deren preisw├╝rdiger Ungest├╝m die Speisen und St├дrkungen erraffen soll! Der Wagenlenker findet noch Gut dazu.

+Grassmann

Sie, deren Andrang grade geht, um zu ergreifen Speis’ und Trank; Durch Suchen nur erlangt das Gut der Opfernde.

+Jamison Brereton

shining one,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take abhikhy─Б╠Бin the sense of тАШglanceтАЩ rather than тАШappearanceтАЩ (as Grassmann, Renou, and Scarlatta 99 do). The finite forms of abh├н тИЪkhy─Б all have the meaning тАШlook atтАЩ, as do the 2 occurrences of the gerund abhikhy─Б╠Бya (I.155.5, II.30.9). abhikhy─Б╠Бoccurs 3 times (here + I.148.5, X.112.10, all compatible with a meaning тАШglanceтАЩ [pace Grassmann]). It may either be the instr. sg. of a root noun or (with AiG II.2.782) a haplologized form of the gerund abhikhy─Б╠Бya. Both possibilities are considered by Scarlatta (98-99).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬProceed, Agni, with pious praises, offering in due order the oblations (to the gods), for you are theirmessenger, the bearer of oblations.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Agni, drive (to the gods) with our good lauds, pouring oblations in yourself in the proper sequence,
as you have become our oblation-carrying messenger.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Contra most interpr., I take Agni as driving to the gods to present them with our praises as well as our oblations, rather than coming here (e.g., Renou тАЬarrive avec les belles louangesтАЭ).

The impv. y─Бh├н is accented because it follows an initial voc.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Worship him who is) of wondrous works, who, gladdened (by offerings), is present like a friend, whom(the priests) by their sacrifices, according to their power, render propitious to the worshipper.тАЭ

him, like an ally, well established among the people who abide in truth.

+Griffith

Kind as a friend to men who keep the holy Law.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPious worshippers, at the plural ce of offerings adore with praise him who is gratified by worship, thecompleter of the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Adore with praise: jujuс╣гuс╕е = they have adored; up─Бsevadhvam

+Jamison Brereton

O you (people) who seek truthтАФin him abiding in truth, bringing success to the sacrifice with our hymn,
in him do they [=the gods] take pleasure, in the footprint of our homage.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou explicitly identify the subj. of jujuс╣гuс╕е in c as those seeking truth (voc. с╣Ыt─Бyavaс╕е), the human ritualists addressed in a. Although switch between 2nd and 3rd ps. even within a verse is not rare, I think the gods are the more likely subject, as they generally are to forms of тИЪjuс╣г. This verse depicts the ritual model whereby Agni brings the gods to the ritual ground to receive oblations, with this location specified by n├бmasas pad├й – in contrast to vs. 6, where Agni conveys the oblations and praises to the gods (presumably in heaven), the other model of sacrificial interaction.

+Griffith

Him, true to Law, who perfecteth the sacrifice,. Law-loving ones!
Ye with your song have gratified in the place of prayer.

+Geldner

Den Gesetzestreuen, ihr Gesetzeseifrigen, des Opfers Ausrichter mit Lobrede; an ihm haben sie Wohlgefallen an der St├дtte der Verneigung.

+Grassmann

O fromme preist den heiligen mit Lied den Opferf├╢rderer; Sie haben an der Andachtsst├дtte ihn erfreut.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe с╣Ыс╣гi Vya┼Ыva, desirous (of propitiating) the showerer (of rain), has gratified you, the bestower ofwealth; so we too kindle you for (the acquisition of) ample riches.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The seer Vya┼Ыva, seeking bulls [/Ukс╣гan (=his patron)], pleased you, the finder of goods.
For great wealth might we kindle you.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The point of this verse seems to be that Vya┼Ыva (the poet’s father) got the goods, either directly from Agni or via the patron Ukс╣гan, and we hope this will provide a pattern for us.

The grammatically disharmonious phrase mah├│ r─Бy├й would better be tr.

тАЬgreatly for wealth.тАЭ See disc. ad IV.31.11.

As such may we enkindle thee for ample wealth.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll the consentient gods have made you their messenger, may you, divine Agni, who are the first (of thedeities), quickly become the object of their worship.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May you: may you quickly become worthy of the sacrifice,(as bearing our oblations to them)

+Jamison Brereton

Because all the gods, altogether, made you their messenger,
by harkening (to them), o god, you became the first one worthy of the sacrifice.

+Griffith

All Deities of one accord appointed thee their messenger:
Thou, God, through hearing, hadst first claim to sacrifice.

+Geldner

Denn alle G├╢tter haben einm├╝tig dich zu ihrem Boten gemacht. Durch deine Bereitwilligkeit wardst du, Gott, der erste Opferw├╝rdige.

+Grassmann

Denn alle G├╢tter setzten dich vereint zu ihrem Boten ein, Du warst sogleich der erste Opferer, o Gott.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬс╣Ъс╣гi, son of Vya┼Ыva, adore the far-spreading domestic Agni, with praises, like Sth┼лray┼лpa.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sth┼лray┼лpa is said to be the name of a с╣Ыс╣гi

+Jamison Brereton

Now chant to him of extensive power with praise songs like sturdy posts [/like Sth┼лray┼лpa],
o seer, son of Vya┼ЫvaтАФto the Agni of the household.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax sth┼лray┼лpav├бt may be a pun. On the one hand, formations of this sort, with neut. -v├бt suffix, generally mean тАШlike XтАЩ, тАШas X didтАЩ, with X a PN. The presence of an undoubted ex. in the same position in the immediately preceding vs., vya┼Ыvav├бt тАШlike Vya┼ЫvaтАЩ, strongly supports this interpr. The poet addressed by the impv. arca is being urged to chant тАШlike Sth┼лray┼лpaтАЩ. Grassmann and Renou interpr. the form thus. But sth┼лray┼лpa- also has lexical meaning, тАШ(having?) sturdy postsтАЩ (in the absence of accent we cannot tell whether the cmpd is a bahuvr─лhi or a karmadh─Бraya).

The y┼лpa is both the post to which the animal to be sacrificed is tethered and a crucial post or beam in the construction of dwellings. In this lexical meaning the comparison could either be between the praise songs and sturdy posts or someone who possesses them, or between Agni and the post or post-possessor. Note that it is Agni d├бmya- (тАШof the householdтАЩ) who receives the chant. If the comparison is to the praise songs, they would be conceptualized as the uprights that help make the house solid. The parallel adduced by Geldner, I.51.14 тАж st├│mo d├║ryo n├б y┼л╠Бpaс╕е тАЬa praise-song like a door-post,тАЭ is particularly apt. This is the sense reflected in my tr. and also in GeldnerтАЩs and assumes a karmadh─Бraya. If the comparison is to Agni, a bahuvr─лhi would be better: тАЬto Agni of the household, like one [=a house] having sturdy posts.тАЭ The kinship asserted between Agni and trees in the next verse may give some support to this last interpr.

+Griffith

Now sing, as Sthurayupa sang, with lands to him who spreadeth far,
To Agni of the home, O Rsi, Vyasva’s son.

+Geldner

Sing jetzt den Vollkr├дftigen mit Lobliedern zu, die einem festen Pfosten gleichen, dem h├дuslichen Agni, o Rishi, Sohn des Vyasva!

+Grassmann

Jetzt singe dem gewaltigen mit Lied nach Sthurajupa’s Art Dem Hauses Feuer, S├дnger du, Via├зva’s Sohn.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSit down, Agni, on the sacred grass, in the presence of all those worshippers diligent (in pious works,induced) by their veneration (to accept) the oblations of men.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Because he, the great one, is superior to all, (let) the oblations of the descendants of Manu (also be) superior.
O Agni, sit down on the ritual grass with homage.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntax of this vs. is very difficult; Renou even suggests that it consists of fragments тАЬnon syntaxis├йsтАЭ – a coinage I would like to introduce to English. The standard interpr. take the NP in p─Бda a as acc. pl., more (Oldenberg) or less (Geldner) parallel to havy─Б╠Бni in b and then either supply a verb to govern them (Geldner: тАЬbring [X to Y]тАЭ) or cobble together a very implausible syntactic bond between the verb n├н satsi in c and the accusatives in ab (e.g., Renou тАЬEn direction de tous … assieds toiтАЭ). I take a very different route, first by interpr. mah├бс╕е тАж sat├бс╕е not as acc. pl. but gen./abl. sg. This phrase seems to have some special status: cf. I.36.3 mah├бs te sat├бс╕е тАЬsince you are great,тАЭ same phrase in VIII.101.11 тАЬof you who are great.тАЭ I take the referent of the abl./gen. phrase to be Agni, and I also interpr. abh├н с╣гat├бс╕е in the usual idiomatic meaning of abh├н тИЪas тАШbe superior toтАЩ, construed here with the acc. v├н┼Ыv─Бn. In b I simply supply a different form of the root тИЪas, namely santu, to be construed with the abh├н in the same meaning. The point of the sentence is that since Agni, who is superior to everything, is our Hotar and the conduit of our offerings to the gods, our oblations cannot help being superior as well.

+Griffith

For men’s oblations brought to him who is the mighty Lord of all,
Sit, Agni, mid our homage, on the sacred grass.

+Geldner

F├╝r die alle ├╝berragenden Gro├Яen bring die menschlichen Opfergaben! Agni, setz dich unter Verneigung auf das Barhis!

+Grassmann

Zu all den grossen, m├дchtigen und zu des Menschen Opferwerk, O Agni, setz dich auf die Streu gebetumt├╢nt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are renowned, bring hither the truthful, the purely vigorous, the resplendent deities Mitra andVaruс╣Зa.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are ordinarily associated with Agni at sacrifices

+Jamison Brereton

Agni, you are glorious. Convey Mitra and Varuс╣Зa here,
the sovereign kings possessing the truth and of refined skill.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The abrupt introduction of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa may look forward to the next hymn but one, VIII.25, devoted at least in its first part, to these two gods. The last p─Бda of the first verse of VIII.25 (с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Бn─Б yajase put├бdakс╣гas─Б) is almost identical to the last p─Бda here (с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Бn─Б samr─Б╠Бj─Б put├бdakс╣гas─Б).

+Griffith

Thou, Agni, art a glorious God: bring hither Mitra, Varuna,
Imperial Sovrans, holy-minded, true to Law.

+Geldner

Agni, du bist der Angesehene; fahr uns Mitra und Varuna her, die gesetzestreuen Opferherren von lauterem Wollen!

+Grassmann

Du, o Agni, bist mit Glanz begabt; fahre Mitra und Varuna her, die heiligen, reingesinnten Oberherrn.

+Elizarenkova
